# CHARACTERISTICS OF STUDIES

# Characteristics of included studies [ordered by year of study]

HIFI 1989  

<table><tr><td>Methods</td><td>Multicentre (11) randomised controlled trial</td></tr><tr><td>Participants</td><td>Inclusion criteria: 
- birth weight 750 to 2000 g 
- respiratory failure in first 24 hrs of life; those at 1250 to 2000 g only eligible if severe RDS 
- receiving &lt; 12 hrs of mechanical ventilation 
Exclusion criteria: meconium aspiration; neuromuscular disease; hydrops fetalis; major congenital malformations; hypoplastic lungs 
Stratification: by centre; by birth weight (from 750 to 1500 g in 250 g strata, 1501 to 2000 g in single stratum) 
673 infants enrolled (12 withdrawals, died or consent withdrawn before treated) 
Mean gestational age: 28.4 ± 2.3 wk in HFOV, 28.3 ± 2.2 in CV 
Mean birth weight: 1092 ± 294 g in HFOV, 1087 ± 281 g in CV 
Antenatal corticosteroids: not reported</td></tr></table>

Risk of bias  

<table><tr><td colspan="2">HIFI 1989 (Continued)</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Mean age at randomisation: 6.1 ± 4.6 hrs in HFOV, 5.8 ± 4.0 hrs in CV</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="7">Interventions</td><td>HFOV: OSC using Hummingbird. Settings: initial MAP same or below MAP on CV, 15 Hz</td></tr><tr><td>HVS: no. Hypoxaemia first treated by increasing FiO2, and thereafter by increasing MAP</td></tr><tr><td>CV: IMV. Settings: rate 20 to 40/min, IT 0.3 to 1.0 sec, PIP 20 to 25 cmH2O, PEEP 2 to 5 cm H2O.</td></tr><tr><td>LPS: no.</td></tr><tr><td>Target PCO2: 35 to 60 mmHg</td></tr><tr><td>Duration of assigned treatment: until extubation, unless infant meets failure criteria</td></tr><tr><td>Cross-over: if infants meet failure criteria (failure to oxygenate or ventilate adequately with assigned ventilator)</td></tr><tr><td>Outcomes</td><td>Chronic lung disease (CLD) = oxygen therapy at 28 days and abnormal chest x-ray; mortality at 28 days; pulmonary air leak (± pneumothorax); all IVH; grade 3 and 4 IVH; PVL; mechanical ventilation at 28 days; failure of assigned treatment (PaO2 &lt; 45 mmHg or PaCO2 &gt; 65 mmHg; NEC; use of vasopressors; pulmonary function at 9 months (432, 82% of survivors); neurodevelopmental outcome at 16 to 24 months (386, 74% of survivors)</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="3">Notes</td><td>Surfactant: not used (not available)</td></tr><tr><td>Cross-over: 26% in HFOV, 17% in CV</td></tr><tr><td>Postnatal corticosteroids: 12% in HFOV, 9% in CV</td></tr></table>

<table><tr><td>Bias</td><td>Authors&#x27; judgement</td><td>Support for judgement</td></tr><tr><td>Random sequence generation (selection bias)</td><td>Low risk</td><td>Quote: &quot;computer generated randomisation scheme&quot;</td></tr><tr><td>Allocation concealment (selection bias)</td><td>Unclear risk</td><td>No information on randomisation procedure</td></tr><tr><td>Blinding of participants and personnel (performance bias)
All outcomes</td><td>High risk</td><td>Blinding was not possible for care-givers and not relevant for patients</td></tr><tr><td>Blinding of outcome assessment (detection bias)
All outcomes</td><td>Unclear risk</td><td>Blinding of outcome assessment was not relevant for most outcomes (death, oxygen dependency). No information on blinding for other outcomes</td></tr><tr><td>Incomplete outcome data (attrition bias)
All outcomes</td><td>Low risk</td><td>Complete follow-up for primary outcome (CLD, 98.3%); completeness of follow-up for longer-term outcomes: 74% to 82%</td></tr></table>

Clark 1992  

<table><tr><td>Methods</td><td>Single centre randomised controlled trial</td></tr><tr><td>Participants</td><td>Inclusion criteria:</td></tr></table>

# Clark 1992 (Continued)

Risk of bias  

<table><tr><td></td><td>- gestational age &lt; 35 weeks
- birth weight &lt; 1751 g
- requiring mechanical ventilation
- younger than 24 hours
Exclusion criteria: positive blood culture; lethal congenital anomaly; hydrops fetalis; congenital diagrammatic hernia
Stratification: by birth weight: &lt; 1001 versus 1001 to 1750 g; by age: 0 to 12 versus 12 to 24 hrs
152 infants eligible, 98 (63%) enrolled: 78% inborn; RDS chest x-ray score at entry HFOV &gt; CV; 15 post-randomisation exclusions in publication - data retrieved from author
Mean gestational age: 28 ± 3 wk in HFOV and in CV
Mean birth weight: 1080 ± 310 g in HFOV, 1080 ± 340 g in CV
Antenatal corticosteroids: 12% in HFOV and 13% in CV
Mean age at randomisation: 7 hrs in HFOV, 9 hrs in CV</td></tr><tr><td>Interventions</td><td>HFOV: OSC using Sensormedics 3100. Settings: MAP 1 to 2 cm H2O higher than CV, 10 Hz, I:E ratio 1:2
HVS: yes; increase MAP to optimise oxygenation, wean FiO2first, once FiO2&lt; 0.6 priority to wean MAP
CV: time-cycled, pressure-limited ventilation; no synchronisation. Settings: IT 0.3 to 0.6 sec, rate 25 to 40/min, PEEP 4 to 6 cm H2O, PIP 20 to 27 cm H2O
LPS: no
Target PCO2: 35 to 55 mmHg
Duration of assigned treatment: HFOV until extubation
Cross-over: balanced crossover design, offering patients failing to respond to the assigned mode a trial of the alternative mode. Failure criteria: failure to maintain adequate oxygenation (PO2&gt;50 mmHg) or ventilation (PCO2&gt;60 mmHg) for 3 hrs</td></tr><tr><td>Outcomes</td><td>Chronic lung disease (CLD) = oxygen therapy at 30 days + abnormal chest x-ray; oxygen therapy at 36 weeks postmenstrual age; failure of assigned treatment to maintain PaO2&gt;50 mmHg or PaCO2&lt; 60 mmHg or in CV group development of pulmonary air leak; pulmonary air leak (± pneumothorax); all IVH; grades 3 or 4 IVH; mortality at 30 days</td></tr><tr><td>Notes</td><td>Surfactant: no (not available)
Cross-over: 9% in HFOV, 35% in CV
Postnatal corticosteroids: not reported
Additional arm to the trial consisted of HFOV for 72 hrs then switch to CV (not analysed here)</td></tr></table>

<table><tr><td>Bias</td><td>Authors' judgement</td><td>Support for judgement</td></tr><tr><td>Random sequence generation (selection bias)</td><td>Low risk</td><td>Quote: "random cards"</td></tr><tr><td>Allocation concealment (selection bias)</td><td>Unclear risk</td><td>Quote: "blind draw"</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3">Clark 1992 (Continued)</td></tr><tr><td>Blinding of participants and personnel (performance bias)
All outcomes</td><td>High risk</td><td>Blinding was not possible for care-givers and not relevant for patients</td></tr><tr><td>Blinding of outcome assessment (detection bias)
All outcomes</td><td>Unclear risk</td><td>Blinding of outcome assessment was not relevant for most outcomes (death, oxygen dependency). No information on outcomes such as brain ultrasound</td></tr><tr><td>Incomplete outcome data (attrition bias)
All outcomes</td><td>Low risk</td><td>Complete follow-up (after additional data from author)</td></tr></table>

Ogawa 1993  

<table><tr><td>Methods</td><td>Multicentre (9) randomised controlled trial</td></tr><tr><td>Participants</td><td>Inclusion criteria: 
- birth weight 750 to 2000 g 
- requiring mechanical ventilation soon after birth 
Exclusion criteria: if &gt; 12 hrs old; presence of IVH within 1 hr after birth for inborns and within 6 hrs for transferred babies 
Stratification: by birth weight (750 to 1249 g, 1250 to 1999 g) 
92 infants enrolled and analysed 
Mean gestational age: 29 ± 2.3 wk in HFOV, 29 ± 2.1 in CV 
Mean birth weight: 1243 ± 322 g in HFOV, 1250 ± 318 g in CV 
Antenatal corticosteroids: not reported 
Mean age at randomisation: 2.0 ± 1.6 hrs in HFOV, 1.7 ± 1.5 hrs in CV</td></tr><tr><td>Interventions</td><td>HFOV: OSC using Hummingbird. Settings: high initial MAP, 15 Hz 
HVS: yes. Alveolar recruitment by manual bagging and use of high MAP. Target FiO2 not reported 
CV: pressure-limited time-cycled, method not stated, using Bear Cub or Sechrist 
Target PCO2: 35 to 50 mmHg 
Duration of assigned treatment: not reported 
Cross-over: allowed if infant meets failure criteria (same as in HIFI trial)</td></tr><tr><td>Outcomes</td><td>Primary outcome all IVH and grade 3 or 4 IVH; chronic lung disease (CLD) = oxygen therapy at 28 days and abnormal chest x-ray; mortality at 28 days; failure of assigned treatment (as for HIFI 1989); pulmonary air leak; PVL; mechanical ventilation at 28 days; duration of mechanical ventilation; neurodevelopmental outcome at 12 months (all survivors)</td></tr><tr><td>Notes</td><td>Surfactant: bovine surfactant given in case of &quot;clinical diagnosis of RDS&quot;; 78% of infants received surfactant in both groups 
Cross-over: 9% in HFOV, 2% in CV</td></tr></table>

Ogawa 1993 (Continued)

Postnatal corticosteroids: not reported

Risk of bias  

<table><tr><td>Bias</td><td>Authors&#x27; judgement</td><td>Support for judgement</td></tr><tr><td>Random sequence generation (selection bias)</td><td>Unclear risk</td><td>Quote: &quot;eligible for randomisation&quot;</td></tr><tr><td>Allocation concealment (selection bias)</td><td>Low risk</td><td>Quote: &quot;randomisation with opaque envelopes&quot;</td></tr><tr><td>Blinding of participants and personnel (performance bias) 
All outcomes</td><td>High risk</td><td>Blinding was not possible for care-givers and not relevant for patients</td></tr><tr><td>Blinding of outcome assessment (detection bias) 
All outcomes</td><td>Unclear risk</td><td>Blinding of outcome assessment was not relevant for most outcomes (death, oxygen dependency). No information on blinding of assessment of head ultra-sound or chest x-ray</td></tr><tr><td>Incomplete outcome data (attrition bias) 
All outcomes</td><td>Low risk</td><td>Complete follow-up for primary outcome and for long-term follow-up</td></tr></table>

Gerstmann 1996  

<table><tr><td>Methods</td><td>Multicentre (3) randomised controlled trial</td></tr><tr><td>Participants</td><td>Inclusion criteria: 
- gestational age &lt; 36 wk 
- requiring mechanical ventilation shortly after birth 
- at least moderate respiratory insufficiency (Pa/AO2&lt; 0.5; poor ventilation) 
Exclusion criteria: patients &gt; 12 hrs old; severe congenital defects; pre-existing air leak 
Stratification: by birth weight (≤ 1000 g, &gt;1000 g); by age at randomisation (≤ 4 hrs, &gt;4hrs) 
125 infants enrolled 
Mean gestational age: 30.8 ± 2.2 wk in HFOV, 30.1 ± 2.7 wk in CV 
Mean birth weight: 1560 ± 460 g in HFOV, 1460 ± 470 in CV 
Antenatal corticosteroids: 30% in HFOV, 18% in CV 
Mean age at randomisation: mean 2.9 hrs (range 2.4 to 3.3) in HFOV, mean 2.0 hrs (range 1.4 to 3.0) in CV</td></tr><tr><td>Interventions</td><td>HFOV: OSC using Sensormedics 3100(A). Settings: initial MAP 1 to 2 cm H2O &gt; with CV, I:E ratio 0.33, 10 to 15 Hz 
HVS: yes. Increase MAP to improve oxygenation with target FiO2&lt; 0.30 
CV: IMV using Sechrist. Synchronisation: no. Settings: IT 0.35 to 0.55 sec, rate &lt; 60/min, PEEP 3 to 7 cm H2O, PIP up to 30 cm H2O if &lt; 1 kg and up to 35 cm H2O if &gt; 1 kg</td></tr></table>

# Gerstmann 1996 (Continued)

LPS: no

Target  $\mathsf{PCO}_2$  35 to  $45\mathrm{mmHg}$

Duration of assigned treatment: HFOV until extubation or switched to CV if insufficient respiratory drive

Cross-over: if infants meet failure criteria (insufficient oxygenation or ventilation for  $>2$  hrs; persistent haemodynamic problems; destabilizing problem of air leak; requiring hand ventilation)

<table><tr><td>Outcomes</td><td>Chronic lung disease (CLD) = oxygen therapy at 30 days and abnormal chest x-ray; oxygen at discharge (mean age 37 weeks PMA); mortality at 30 days; failure of assigned treatment (PaO2 &lt; 50 or PaCO2 &gt; 60 mmHg for &gt; 2 hrs, or excessive pressures of IPPV); pulmonary air leak; all IVH; grade 3 or 4 IVH; PVL; mechanical ventilation at 28 days; NEC; use of vasopressors; PDA (treated); ROP; BAER; hospital cost</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="3">Notes</td><td>Surfactant: all infants received at least one dose of bovine surfactant after enrolment in the trial. Infants in the HFOV group received significantly fewer surfactant doses than infants in the CV group</td></tr><tr><td>Cross-over: 2% in HFOV, 15% in CV</td></tr><tr><td>Postnatal corticosteroids: not reported</td></tr></table>

# Risk of bias

<table><tr><td>Bias</td><td>Authors&#x27; judgement</td><td>Support for judgement</td></tr><tr><td>Random sequence generation (selection bias)</td><td>Low risk</td><td>Quote: &quot;Randomisation was by blind card draw from separate sets of...&quot;</td></tr><tr><td>Allocation concealment (selection bias)</td><td>Unclear risk</td><td>Insufficient information regarding concealment procedures</td></tr><tr><td>Blinding of participants and personnel (performance bias)
All outcomes</td><td>High risk</td><td>Blinding was not possible for care-givers and not relevant for patients</td></tr><tr><td>Blinding of outcome assessment (detection bias)
All outcomes</td><td>Low risk</td><td>Blinding of outcome assessment was not relevant for most outcomes (death, oxygen dependency). Neurodevelopmental assessment was blinded</td></tr><tr><td>Incomplete outcome data (attrition bias)
All outcomes</td><td>Low risk</td><td>Complete follow-up for primary outcome. Long-term follow-up of infants of 1 centre: 87% completeness of follow-up</td></tr></table>

# Rettwitz-Volk 1998

<table><tr><td>Methods</td><td>Multicentre (3) randomised controlled trial</td></tr><tr><td>Participants</td><td>Inclusion criteria: 
- birth weight 750 to 1500 g 
- respiratory distress syndrome 
Exclusion criteria: congenital anomalies; hydrops fetalis 
Stratification: by birth weight (750 to 1000 g, 1001 to 1500 g) 
96 infants enrolled and analysed</td></tr></table>

Risk of bias  

<table><tr><td colspan="2">Rettwitz-Volk 1998 (Continued)</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Mean gestational age: 28.5 ± 0.9 wk in HFOV, 28.4 ± 0.95 wk in CV</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Mean birth weight: 1107 ± 112 g in HFOV, 1111 ± 116 g in CV</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Antenatal corticosteroids: 24% in HFOV, 18% in CV</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Mean age at randomisation: 1.16 ± 0.50 hrs in HFOV, 0.66 ± 0.33 hrs in CV</td></tr><tr><td>Interventions</td><td>HFOV: OSC using Stephan SHF 3000 piston oscillator. Settings: initial MAP and amplitude to show good chest movements, 15 to 20 Hz, I:E ratio 1:1</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>HVS: no. Weaning of MAP first</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>CV: IMV using Stephan HF 300 or Dräger Babylog 8000. Synchronisation: not reported. Settings: PIP to show good chest expansion, IT 0.25 to 0.45 sec, I:E at least = 1:2, PEEP 3 to 4 cm H2O</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>LPS: no</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Target PCO2: 35 to 48 mmHg</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Duration of assigned treatment: until extubation or allowed switched to CV if FiO2&lt; 0.30 and MAP 3 to 4 cm H2O</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Cross-over: allowed if infant meets failure criteria (inadequate oxygenation of ventilation with assigned mode; for patients on CV: development of PIE)</td></tr><tr><td>Outcomes</td><td>Mortality before discharge, CLD (O2at 37 weeks PMA), failure of assigned treatment (PaO2&lt; 45 mmHg or PaCO2&gt; 60 mmHg), pulmonary ALS ± pneumothorax, IVH, PVL</td></tr><tr><td>Notes</td><td>Surfactant: bovine surfactant (Suvanta) was administered after randomisation when chest x-ray showed RDS grade II and FiO2&gt; 0.60 was necessary to achieve PO2&gt; 50 mmHg</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Cross-over: 17% in HFOV, 18% in CV</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Postnatal corticosteroids: 43% in HFOV, 60% in CV (all patients still on oxygen therapy at 7 days of age received a 21 day course of dexamethasone)</td></tr></table>

<table><tr><td>Bias</td><td>Authors&#x27; judgement</td><td>Support for judgement</td></tr><tr><td>Random sequence generation (selection bias)</td><td>Low risk</td><td>Quote: &quot;balanced block randomization scheme&quot;</td></tr><tr><td>Allocation concealment (selection bias)</td><td>Unclear risk</td><td>No information on procedures to conceal allocation</td></tr><tr><td>Blinding of participants and personnel (performance bias)
All outcomes</td><td>High risk</td><td>Blinding was not possible for care-givers and not relevant for patients</td></tr><tr><td>Blinding of outcome assessment (detection bias)
All outcomes</td><td>Unclear risk</td><td>Blinding of outcome assessment was not relevant for most outcomes (death, oxygen dependency). No information on assessment of head ultrasound or chest x-ray</td></tr><tr><td>Incomplete outcome data (attrition bias)
All outcomes</td><td>Low risk</td><td>Complete follow-up for primary endpoint</td></tr></table>

Thome 1998  

<table><tr><td>Methods</td><td>Multicentre (6) randomised controlled trial</td></tr><tr><td>Participants</td><td>Inclusion criteria: 
- inborn 
- gestational age 24 to 29 wk 
- requiring mechanical ventilation within 6 hrs of birth 
Exclusion criteria: major congenital or chromosomal anomalies, hydrops fetalis 
Stratification: by centre; by gestational age (24 to 25 wk, 26 to 27 wk, 28 to 29 wk) 
289 infants enrolled; 4 infants excluded because of congenital malformation and 1 infant excluded be-cause of pneumothorax before randomisation; 284 infants analysed 
Median (range) gestational age: 27.0 wk (23.4 to 29.9 wk) in HFOV, 27.3 wk (24.0 to 29.9 wk) in CV 
Median (range) birth weight: 888 g (420 to 1830 g) in HFOV, 870 g (370 to 1395 g) in CV 
Antenatal corticosteroids: 81% in HFOV, 86% in CV 
Median (range) age at intubation: 12 minutes (0 to 360) both in HFOV and in CV 
Median (range) duration of positive pressure ventilation before randomisation: 28 minutes (0 to 90) in HFOV, 0 minutes (0 to 90) in CV</td></tr><tr><td>Interventions</td><td>HFOV: HFFI using Infant Star ventilator (software version 83). Settings: initial MAP 1 to 2 cm H2O higher than with CV or 10 to 12 cm H2O if HFV started immediately, 10 Hz 
HVS: yes. Stepwise increase of MAP until target FiO2&lt; 0.30 is reached. Mild sustained inflations (MAP +5 cm H2O during 15 sec) after tracheal suctioning 
CV: IPPV time-cycled pressure-limited ventilation using various ventilators (Dräger Babylog 8000, Stephan HF300, Infant Star, Sechrist IV-100B). Settings: initial rates 60 to 80/min, aimed at lower PIP and PEEP ≥ 3 cm H2O 
LPS: yes 
Target PCO2: 40 to 60 mmHg, up to 70 mmHg from day 7 
Duration of assigned treatment: until extubation or for 10 days 
Cross-over: in first 10 days allowed if infant meets failure criteria (air leak, oxygenation index as defined in primary outcome), decision left to the attending physician</td></tr><tr><td>Outcomes</td><td>&quot;Treatment failure&quot; (ALS &lt; 10 days, oxygenation index &gt; 35 , 40 or 45 in the 3 gestation strata, CLD at 36 weeks or death before discharge), CLD = oxygen or ventilatory support at 36 weeks, ALS = PIE or gross air leaks; IVH; PVL; ROP</td></tr><tr><td>Notes</td><td>Surfactant: if FiO2was &gt; 0.30 in HFOV group, or &gt; 0.40 in CV group. Bovine or porcine surfactant given to 68% of HFOV and 71% of CV 
Cross-over: not reported 
Postnatal corticosteroids: 39% of HFOV, 41% of CV</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2">Risk of bias</td></tr></table>

Mean birth weight:

Moriette 2001  

<table><tr><td>Methods</td><td>Multicentre (10) randomised controlled trial</td></tr><tr><td>Participants</td><td>Inclusion criteria: 
- gestational age 24 to 29 wk 
- requiring mechanical ventilation before 6 hrs of life

Use of &gt; 1 dose of surfactant 
Pulmonary air leak (PIE and pneumothorax) 
ROP (? grade) 
CLD (oxygen at 28 days and oxygen at 36 weeks 
Duration of IPPV, O2 therapy, hospitalisation 
Grade 3/4 IVH (7 to 10 day ultrasound (U/S))</td></tr></table>

Van Reempts 2003  

<table><tr><td>Methods</td><td>Single centre randomised controlled trial</td></tr><tr><td>Participants</td><td>Inclusion criteria: 
- gestational age &lt; 32 wk 
- less than 6 hrs old 
- requiring mechanical ventilation 
- FiO2&gt; 0.40 or MAP x FiO2&gt; 3.8 
- chest x-ray compatible with RDS 
Exclusion criteria: active infection at birth, congenital anomalies 
Stratification: not reported 
300 infants enrolled and analysed. 
Mean gestational age: 28.5 ± 1.8 wk in HFOV, 28.8 ± 1.9 in CV 
Mean birth weight: 1173 ± 346 g in HFOV, 1217 ± 363 g in CV 
Antenatal corticosteroids: 63% in HFOV, 66% in CV 
Median (range) age at randomisation: 0.93 hrs (0.33 to 24.9 hrs) in HFOV, 0.88 hrs (0.33 to 24.8 hrs) in CV</td></tr><tr><td>Interventions</td><td>HFOV: mix of OSC using Sensormedics 3100A (122 infants) and HFFI using Infant Star (25 infants). Settings: initial MAP 8 cm H2O if &lt; 29 weeks and 10 cm H2O if 29 to 31 weeks, 10 Hz. 
HVS: yes. Increase MAP to improve oxygenation and wean FiO2. Target FiO2 not reported</td></tr></table>

# Van Reempts 2003 (Continued)

CV: IMV using Dräger Babylog 8000 (73 infants) or Infant Star (80 infants). Synchronisation: not reported. Settings: PIP 20 cm H₂O (aim low), PEEP 4 cm H₂O, IT < 0.35 sec, rate 80/min, l:E ratio1: 1.1

LPS: yes

Target  $\mathsf{PCO}_2$  : 35 to  $45\mathrm{mmHg}$

Duration of assigned treatment: preferentially HFOV until extubation, unless failure of weaning (criteria described) in which case infants were switched to CV

Crossover: infant was changed to alternative mode if failure criteria were met (one of the following: 1) inadequate oxygenation or ventilation, as described in the trial, in the first 7 days of life, 2) uncontrollable air leak, 3) cardiovascular dysfunction, 4) need for hand ventilation to maintain adequate gas exchange)

<table><tr><td>Outcomes</td><td>Chronic lung disease (CLD - on O2 or assisted ventilation) at 36 weeks, death before discharge, failure of assigned treatment, CLD at 28 days, pulmonary interstitial air, pneumothorax, intraventricular haemorrhage, periventricular leukomalacia, retinopathy of prematurity, days of IPPV or CPAP or O2, developmental outcome in early childhood for infants &lt; 30 weeks or with an abnormal head ultrasound</td></tr></table>

Notes

Surfactant: after initial stabilization either on CV or on HFOV, all infants were given surfactant (Alveofact or Suvanta)

Cross-over:  $12\%$  in HFOV,  $7\%$  in CV

Postnatal corticosteroids: not reported

Author provided additional information on grades of ROP, prenatal steroids and neonatal mortality

# Risk of bias

<table><tr><td>Bias</td><td>Authors&#x27; judgement</td><td>Support for judgement</td></tr><tr><td>Random sequence generation (selection bias)</td><td>Unclear risk</td><td>Quote: &quot;were randomised&quot;</td></tr><tr><td>Allocation concealment (selection bias)</td><td>Unclear risk</td><td>Quote: &quot;using sealed folded papers&quot;</td></tr><tr><td>Blinding of participants and personnel (performance bias) 
All outcomes</td><td>High risk</td><td>Blinding was not possible for care-givers and not relevant for patients</td></tr><tr><td>Blinding of outcome assessment (detection bias) 
All outcomes</td><td>Low risk</td><td>Blinding of outcome assessment was not relevant for most outcomes (death, oxygen dependency). Blinding was applied for grading of chronic lung disease, intracranial haemorrhage, periventricular leukomalacia and retinopathy of prematurity</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="2">Incomplete outcome data (attrition bias) 
All outcomes</td><td rowspan="2">Low risk</td><td>Complete follow-up for primary outcome</td></tr><tr><td>For long-term outcome: only 57% follow-up for HFOV, and 51% follow-up for CV</td></tr></table>

Vento 2005  

<table><tr><td>Methods</td><td>Single centre randomised controlled trial</td></tr><tr><td>Participants</td><td>Inclusion criteria: 
- inborn 
- birth weight 500 to 1500 g 
- gestational age 24 to 29 wk 
- requiring intubation at birth and ongoing intensive care 
Exclusion criteria: congenital malformations, prenatal infections 
Stratification: not reported 
42 infants eligible; 2 infants excluded with congenital pneumonia; 40 infants enrolled and analysed 
Mean gestational age: 27.1 ± 1.4 wk in HFOV, 27.4 ± 1.2 wk in CV 
Mean birth weight: 882 ± 157 g in HFOV, 936 ± 285 g in CV 
Antenatal corticosteroids: any steroids in 100% in HFOV and 90% in CV, complete course of steroids in 55% in HFVO and 60% in CV 
Mean age at randomisation: all infants were randomised within 30 minutes of life</td></tr><tr><td>Interventions</td><td>HFOV: HFFI using Dräger Babylog 8000+. Settings: initial MAP 2 cm H2O higher than with CV or at 10 cm H2O, 10 Hz 
HVS: yes. Increase MAP to improve oxygenation and wean FiO2with target &lt; 0.25 
CV: SIMV using Dräger Babylog 8000+. Setting: Vt 4-6 ml/kg, PEEP 4 to 5 cm H2O, TI 0.30 to 0.40 sec, maximum rate 60/min, PIP weaned first 
LPS: yes. 
Target PCO2: 45 to 55 mmHg 
Duration of assigned treatment: HFOV until extubation 
Cross-over: no</td></tr><tr><td>Outcomes</td><td>Death before discharge, CLD (O2therapy at 36 weeks PMA), pneumothorax, PIE, IVH grades 3 or 4, PVL, ROP &gt; stage 2</td></tr><tr><td>Notes</td><td>Surfactant: 75% of infants in both groups received surfactant. Criteria are not described 
Cross-over: 0% in both groups</td></tr></table>

Salvo 2012  

<table><tr><td>Methods</td><td>Multicentre (3) randomised controlled trial</td></tr><tr><td>Participants</td><td>Inclusion criteria: 
- birth weight &lt; 1500 g 
- gestational age &lt; 30 wk 
- no antenatal corticosteroids 
- requiring mechanical ventilation for RDS within first 2 hrs of life 
Exclusion criteria: major congenital malformation; hydrops fetalis; congenital diaphragmatic hernia; congenital pneumonia; multiple pregnancies; congenital heart disease 
Stratification: not reported 
112 infants eligible; 24 infants excluded (3 no consent, 18 not ventilated, 3 congenital pneumonia or malformation); 88 infants enrolled and analysed 
Mean gestational age: 26.4 ± 2.2 wk in HFOV, 26.5 ± 3.2 wk in CV 
Mean birth weight: 869 ± 266 g in HFOV, 913 ± 224 g in CV 
Antenatal corticosteroids: 0% (exclusion criterion) 
Mean age at randomisation: not reported; all infants were randomised within 2 hrs of birth</td></tr><tr><td>Interventions</td><td>HFOV: OSC using Sensormedics 3100A. Settings: initial MAP 6 to 8 cm H2O, 15 Hz, I:E ratio 1:2, amplitude producing visible chest vibrations 
HVS: yes. Lung volume recruitment as described by De Jaegere 2006. Target FiO2&lt; 0.30 
CV: SIMV using Bear Cub 750 PSV. Settings: PIP 18 to 24 cm H2O, PEEP 5 to 8 cm H2O, IT 0.30 to 0.40 sec, rate 40 to 60/min 
LPS: yes 
Target PCO2&lt; 65 mmHg 
Duration of assigned treatment: HFOV until extubation 
Crossover: switch to alternative mode permitted but not mandatory if failure criteria are met (inadequate oxygenation or ventilation as described in trial protocol; signs of decreased cardiac output)</td></tr><tr><td>Outcomes</td><td>Primary outcomes were: the length of ventilatory support, the need of reintubation, and the length of nasal continuous positive airway pressure support in the postextubation period. Secondary outcomes were: the length of stay in neonatal intensive care unit and in hospital, death before discharge, adverse short- and long-term pulmonary and neonatal outcomes, and the need for a second dose of surfactant and of postnatal glucocorticoid treatment</td></tr><tr><td>Notes</td><td>Surfactant: all infants received surfactant (Curosurf, 200 mg/kg) at a mean postnatal age of 47 min for the HFOV group and 44 min for the CV group 
Cross-over: 1 infant out of 44 in each group 
Postnatal corticosteroids: 1 of 39 infants (2.5%) in HFOV, 4 of 39 infants (10.2%) in CV</td></tr></table>

Sun 2014  

<table><tr><td>Methods</td><td>Multicentre (2) randomised controlled trial</td></tr><tr><td>Participants</td><td>Inclusion Criteria: 
- gestational age &lt; 32 wks 
- birth weight &lt; 1500 g 
- less than 24 hours of age 
- requiring mechanical ventilation for RDS 
- PaO2/FiO2 ratio &lt; 200 mmHg 
- Radiograph criteria of severe RDS 
Exclusion criteria: genetic metabolic diseases, congenital abnormalities, pneumothorax, IVH grade 3 to 4 
Stratification: by centre; by gender; by gestational age (&lt; 28 wk, ≥ 28 wk) 
366 infants eligible and randomised; 3 infants excluded post-randomisation (congenital heart disease); 7 dropouts; 356 infants analysed 
Mean gestational age: 29.3 ± 2.5 wk in HFOV, 29.5 ± 2.3 in CV 
Mean birth weight: 1129 ± 199 g in HFOV, 1117 ± 241 g in CV 
Antenatal corticosteroids: 77% in HFOV, 73% in CV 
Mean age at randomisation: 5.8 ± 5.0 hrs in HFOV, 5.9 ± 5.1 in CV</td></tr><tr><td>Interventions</td><td>HFOV: OSC using SLE5000. Settings: initial MAP 6 to 8 cm H2O and progressively increased, 10 Hz, IT set at default level of ventilator (I:E ratio not reported)</td></tr></table>

Sun 2014 (Continued)  

<table><tr><td></td><td>HVS: yes. Lung volume recruitment as described by De Jaegere 2006. Target FiO2&lt; 0.25</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>CV: SIMV with pressure-support (SIMV-PS) using Servo-i-Maquet. Settings: Vt 4 to 6 ml/kg, PIP needed to achieve chest expansion, PEEP 4 to 6 cm H2O, IT 0.25 to 0.40 sec, rate ≤ 60/min (typically 30 to 40/min plus PS)</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>LPS: yes</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Target PCO2: 40 to 55 mmHg</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Duration of assigned treatment: HFOV until extubation</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Cross-over: no</td></tr><tr><td>Outcomes</td><td>Primary outcomes were mortality or incidence of BPD. A subsequent dose was administered 12 hours after the first dose if PaO2/FiO2was &lt; 200</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Cross-over: 0% in both groups</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Postnatal corticosteroids: not reported</td></tr></table>

Risk of bias

$\mathsf{HFOV} =$  high-frequency oscillatory ventilation;  $\mathsf{OSC} =$  true oscillator; HFFI : high frequency flow interrupter;  $\mathsf{CV} =$  conventional ventilation; (S)IMV = (synchronised) intermittent mandatory ventilation; IT = inspiratory time;  $\mathsf{PIP} =$  positive inspiratory pressure; PEEP = positive end-expiratory pressure;  $\mathsf{MAP} =$  mean airway pressure; CLD = chronic lung disease; ALS = air leak syndrome; IVH = intraventricular haemorrhage;  $\mathsf{PVL} =$  periventricular leukomalacia;  $\mathsf{PMA} =$  postmenstrual age;  $\mathsf{HVS} =$  high volume strategy;  $\mathsf{LPS} =$  lung protective strategy (for CV); Vt = tidal volume

# Characteristics of excluded studies [ordered by study ID]

<table><tr><td>Study</td><td>Reason for exclusion</td></tr><tr><td>Cambonie 2003</td><td>No relevant outcomes</td></tr><tr><td>Froese 1987</td><td>After randomisation of infants (unknown gestation range), 5 of 11 in the HFOV group and an un-known number from the CV group were excluded from the comparisons between treatments</td></tr><tr><td>HiFO 1993</td><td>Rescue treatment with primary aim of preventing pulmonary air leak</td></tr><tr><td>Iscan 2014</td><td>Cross-over trial comparing two modes of HFOV</td></tr><tr><td>Lombet 1996</td><td>A total of 22% excluded after randomisation, mixed population of preterm and term infants</td></tr><tr><td>Nazarchuk 2010</td><td>Prospective randomised trial comparing early HFOV to synchronised intermittent mandatory ventilation (SIMV) in very low birth weight (VLBW) premature infants with omphalocele: 15 infants weighing 501 to 1000 g less than 4 hours of age, who had received one dose of surfactant and required ventilation with mean airway pressure &gt; 4 to 6 cm H2O and FiO2 &gt; 0.25, and had an anticipated duration of ventilation greater than 48 hours. Newborns were stratified by birth weight and prenatal steroid status, and then randomised to either HFOV or SIMV with tidal volume monitoring. Ventilator management for patients in both study arms was strictly governed by protocols that included optimising lung inflation and blood gases, weaning strategies and extubation criteria. 
Not included because of unique underlying condition of enrolled infants (presence of omphalocele)</td></tr><tr><td>Pardou 1993</td><td>Results reported for only 13 (54%) of the 24 subjects randomised to high frequency flow interrupter or CV</td></tr><tr><td>Prashanth 2012</td><td>Prospective, non-randomised comparison of HFOV versus synchronized intermittent mandatory ventilation (SIMV) in 52 preterm infants 26 to 36 weeks&#x27; gestation. The study was excluded because it was not a randomised controlled trial</td></tr><tr><td>Ramanathan 1995</td><td>Mandatory cross-over of treatments at 96 hrs</td></tr><tr><td>Singh 2012</td><td>Randomised controlled trial comparing HFOV (Dräger Babylog Plus) with synchronised intermittent mandatory ventilation (SIMV) in preterm infants with birth weight &gt; 750 g with RDS. The primary outcome was the oxygen index in the first 24 hours. 
In all 53 out of the 215 eligible infants could not be included because of unavailability of the designated ventilator. A total of 150 preterm infants (mean gestational age of 32 weeks) were randomised to receive either HFOV (66 infants) or SIMV (84 infants). After randomisation 40 infants were excluded from the analyses because ventilation was discontinued within 24 hours (17 in the HFOV group and 23 in the SIMV group). The reason for discontinuation was death in 15 cases and &quot;left against medical advice&quot; in 25 cases. HFOV strategy was aimed at recruiting lung volume, and adequate lung inflation was assessed by counting posterior ribs on chest x-ray. SIMV was aimed at keeping tidal volumes low. The study was excluded because of concerns about both selection bias (25% of eligible infants were not included) as well as attrition bias (post-randomisation exclusion of 27% of infants). In addition, clinically relevant outcomes were not measured</td></tr></table>

# Characteristics of studies awaiting assessment [ordered by study ID]

Elazeez 2010  

<table><tr><td>Methods</td><td>Elazeez 2010 conducted a randomised controlled trial to determine differences in regional cerebral blood flow velocity (CBFV) in preterm infants receiving conventional ventilation (CV) versus high frequency oscillatory ventilation (HFOV) using a high-volume strategy</td></tr><tr><td>Participants</td><td>Preterm infants admitted to the NICU at Mansoura University Children&#x27;s Hospital before 12 hours of age. Those requiring ventilator support were randomly allocated to HFOV (n = 23) or CV (n= 24)</td></tr><tr><td>Interventions</td><td>HFOV versus CV</td></tr><tr><td>Outcomes</td><td>Doppler cranial ultrasound and echocardiography were performed on all subjects on day 1 and day 4 with measurements of CBFV in the anterior cerebral (ACA) and middle cerebral arteries (MCA) and assessment of the ductus arteriosus</td></tr><tr><td>Notes</td><td>Published as abstract PAS 2010</td></tr></table>

Sarafidis 2011  

<table><tr><td>Methods</td><td>Sarafidis 2011 conducted a single centre randomised controlled trial to evaluate the effect of optimised synchronized intermittent mandatory ventilation (SIMV) versus high-frequency oscillatory ventilation (HFOV) on circulating CC16 and IL-6 levels</td></tr><tr><td>Participants</td><td>Preterm neonates (gestational age &lt; 30 weeks) requiring mechanical ventilation within the first 2 hrs of life. Of the 30 neonates studied, 24 (gestational age 27.1 ± 1.7 weeks, birth weight (942 ± 214 g) were finally analysed</td></tr><tr><td>Interventions</td><td>Synchronised intermittent mandatory ventilation (SIMV) versus high frequency oscillatory ventilation (HFOV) used as the initial ventilation methods</td></tr><tr><td>Outcomes</td><td>Serum CC16 and IL-6 were measured on establishment of the assigned ventilation mode after admission, at days 3 and 14 of life as well as at 36 weeks postmenstrual age. Demographic-perinatal data and clinical parameters were also recorded</td></tr><tr><td>Notes</td><td></td></tr></table>

# DATA AND ANALYSES

Comparison 1. HFOV versus CV (all trials)

WHAT'S NEW  

<table><tr><td>Date</td><td>Event</td><td>Description</td></tr><tr><td>30 November 2014</td><td>New search has been performed</td><td>Search updated in November 2014.</td></tr><tr><td>30 November 2014</td><td>New citation required and conclusions have changed</td><td>Follow-up study of pulmonary function in adolescents from the trial of Johnson 2002 identified. One new study from China identified (Sun 2014). Conclusions changed to note that the use of elective HFOV compared with CV resulted in a small reduction in the risk of CLD, but that the evidence is weakened by the inconsistency of this effect across trials.</td></tr></table>

As a result of a search update to November 2006, data from four trials have been added. One new trial is still awaiting assessment and another is yet to be published. 
Additional subgroup analyses have been added to explore heterogeneity.</td></tr><tr><td>14 May 2007</td><td>New citation required but conclusions have not changed</td><td>Substantive amendment</td></tr></table>

# CONTRIBUTIONS OF AUTHORS

An earlier version of this review was developed by Bhuta and Henderson-Smart and published in 1996. Both authors were involved at all stages in the review.

In 1999 the review was reformatted by Henderson-Smart with inclusion of two new review authors, Cools and Offringa. Each author evaluated the trials and extracted data independently. Henderson-Smart entered the data and wrote the text while all the co-reviewers contributed to data checking and editing.

The update in 2007 included a search and data extraction from four new trials, by Henderson-Smart and Cools. Henderson-Smart entered the data and edited the review. The review was evaluated by all review authors.

The update in 2009 included a search by Cools and Offringa. Data from the two new trials were extracted by Cools, Offringa and Henderson-Smart. Cools entered the data and edited the review. The review was evaluated by all authors.

The update in 2012 included a search by the CNRG Editorial Office through December 2012. Drs Cools and Offringa reviewed the data from the new trial of Salvo 2012 and edited the review. The review was evaluated by all authors.

The updated search in 2014 identified a follow-up study of pulmonary function from the original trial of Johnson 2002 (Zivanovic, N Engl J Med. 2014 Mar 20;370 (12):1121-30) and a new trial from Sun 2014. Drs Cools and Offringa reviewed the data from the Sun 2014 trial and edited the review.
